  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_949f0976-fee9-415d-931a-04b72b8560c8'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

  <span id="freeText4431312833006162523" style="display:none">ARTEMIS FOWL’S CRIMINAL WAYS HAVE FINALLY GOT THE BETTER OF HIM . . .<br /><br />Young Artemis has frequently used high-tech fairy magic to mastermind the most devious criminal activity of the new century. Now, at a conference in Iceland, Artemis has gathered the fairies to present his latest idea to save the world from global warming.<br /><br />But Artemis is behaving strangely - he seems different. Something terrible has happened to him . . . Artemis Fowl has become nice.<br /><br />The fairies diagnose Atlantis Complex (that’s obsessive compulsive disorder to you and I) - it seems dabbling in magic has damaged Artemis’ main weapon: his mind. Fairy ally Captain Holly Short doesn’t know what to do. The subterranean volcanoes are under attack from vicious robots and Artemis cannot fight them. Can Holly get the real Artemis back before the robot probes destroy every human and life form?<br /><br />This eagerly-awaited adventure is now out in paberback with a fabulous new cover-look to celebrate ten years of Artemis action.</span>

  <span id="freeText13399935957610670916" style="display:none">Artemis Fowl: The Atlantis Complex = Artemis Fowl and the Atlantis Complex (Artemis Fowl, #7), Eoin Colfer<br /><br />Artemis Fowl: The Atlantis Complex is the seventh book in the Artemis Fowl series. It was published on 20 July 2010. <br /><br />It was followed by Artemis Fowl: The Last Guardian, which was confirmed to be the final book in the Artemis Fowl series. <br /><br />The story follows Turnball Root, the criminal brother of Julius Root, breaking out of jail and sending probes to destroy his enemies, including Artemis, his fairy friends, and Butler, whom Artemis sent away due to paranoia being one of the symptoms of Atlantis Complex. <br /><br />After Butler, Artemis, and his fairy friends reunite, along with being saved by Mulch Diggums from a gang of dwarfs sent by Turnball, they hunt down Turnball, tracking him with a computer orb connected to the probes that Artemis found underwater, along with being attacked by a giant, squid-like creature, and find out that Turnball has kidnapped demon warlock N°1 to force him to reverse the aging of Turnball's wife, Leonor. <br /><br /><br />تاریخ نخستین خوانش: روز بیستم ماه آگوست سال 2012 میلادی<br /><br />عنوان: آرتمیس فاول و عقده ی آتلانتیس؛ نویسنده: اوئین (یون، ایون) کالفر؛ مترجم: شیدا رنجبر؛ تهران، افق، 1390، در 452ص؛ شابک 9789643697440؛ چاپ دوم 1390؛ چاپ سوم 1391؛ چاپ چهارم 1393؛ موضوع داستانهای نویسندگان ایرلندی - سده 21م<br /><br />در هفتمین کتاب، «آرتمیس»، احساس گناه میکند و عذاب وجدان‌ دارد، از کارهای خلافی که در بگذشته انجام داده‌ است؛ او دچار بیماری روانی از اجنه می‌شود، که همانند «بیماری‌های وسواس»، «چند شخصیتی»، و «پارانویا» در انسان‌هاست.؛ شخصیت دوم پانزده ساله، که «اوریون» نام دارد، و خیلی هم به نابغه‌ ها نبرده، آشکار می‌شود.؛ او «هالی» را عشق واقعی خویش، و «فلی» را، اسب افسانه‌ ای می‌نامد.؛ در همین جریان، «ترنبال روت»، برادر کوچکتر و خلافکار فرمانده «جولیوس روت»، که زندانی است، تلاش می‌کند آزاد شود، تا به همسر انسانش، که برخلاف اجنه، که صدها سال عمر می‌کنند، پیر شده‌ است، جوانی ابدی بدهد، و «آرتمیس و اریون (شخصیت دوم آرتمیس)» هم، میخواهند و بایستی، از اجرای نقشه ی «ترنبال» جلوگیر کنند، تا باعث نابودی بسیاری از جن و پری‌ها نشود.؛ سایه‌ ای نیز روی ذهن «آرتمیس» افتاده است.؛ پیشتر چیزهایی را میدید، که دیگران نمیدیدند، اما اکنون، چیزهایی را میبیند، که نیستند و وجود خارجی ندارند! درگیری با جن و جادو، به شدت ذهنش را به هم ریخته، و اکنون که روباتهای ویرانگر، به شهر زیرآبی «آتلانتیس»، و جن و پریهایش حمله کرده‌ اند، «آرتمیس فاول» شرور، خوب و دل‌رحم شده، و نمیتواند با آنها بجنگد<br /><br />تاریخ بهنگام رسانی 02/05/1399هجری خورشیدی؛ ا. شربیانی</span>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1384927-daria?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1384927-daria?shelf=beloved-fantasy">beloved-fantasy</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer83755578" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1021460755065447923">After a hideously long stretch without a new Artemis book, <i>Atlantis Complex</i> decides to throw at us....<br/><br/>Psychological disorders!<br/><br/>Giant squids!<br/><br/>Interspecies love! (Aaaw.)<br/><br/>Killer blobs of gel! (Yaay!) <br/><br/>...and much, much more. Colfer's wit is as sharp as ever, the confusing technological banter is utterly welcome, and our characters are back just the way we like 'em. Of course, though, such is not the case with Artemis...<br/><br/>It's nice to know that our current villain is not whom I was expecting, and also tha</span>
  <span id="freeText1021460755065447923" style="display:none">After a hideously long stretch without a new Artemis book, <i>Atlantis Complex</i> decides to throw at us....<br /><br />Psychological disorders!<br /><br />Giant squids!<br /><br />Interspecies love! (Aaaw.)<br /><br />Killer blobs of gel! (Yaay!) <br /><br />...and much, much more. Colfer's wit is as sharp as ever, the confusing technological banter is utterly welcome, and our characters are back just the way we like 'em. Of course, though, such is not the case with Artemis...<br /><br />It's nice to know that our current villain is not whom I was expecting, and also that he/she has a motive other than TAKING OVER THE WORLD!!! This book was layered deeper, and the only fault I found with it was that it was too short. I mean, come on, <i>Time Paradox</i> (which at the moment holds my vote for best book in the series) was at least 200 pages longer. Colfer certainly left loose ends, which will be tied up in the 8th book, which will be the last. (I will weep.) The romance alternated between wince-inducing and tender (works quite well), and I was rather worried for Artemis by the end of the tale, since he's still...well, not all there. <br /><br />But, by and by, another rapid, lively, hilarious and very gung-ho installment in the Artemis Fowl series, who is definitely one of my favourite heroes (or should I say villains?) of all time. Please, Colfer, make the next book nice and long, will you? 600 pages of awesomeness never really hurt anyone. (Hmm. Maybe I should send him fan mail.) <br /><br />PS - Damn you, Hyperion. Who asked you to switch the US covers? They were perfectly fine, and now my shelf pattern is messed up. (Speaking of OCD...hahaha...)<br /><br />PPS - I still want to see Holly end up with Artemis, at least for a book or so. Artemis trumps Trouble every time. Who cares about age and species differences? This book's plot hinted at this possibility anyways, nay? *Holds up huge GO ARTEMIS sign* Colfer, you know this would be awesome. :) Besides, human-elf love seems to be a common trend in fantasty literature. <br /><br />So. *Waits for book 8*</span>
  <a data-text-id="1021460755065447923" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_359202181" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/359202181" />
    <a title="Arun Divakar" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2747498-arun-divakar"><img alt="Arun Divakar" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1253201408p2/2747498.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/359202181?book_show_action=true">Jul 01, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Arun Divakar" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Arun Divakar" href="/user/show/2747498-arun-divakar">Arun Divakar</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer359202181" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1686922933244812043">There was an undeniable freshness to Artemis Fowl and this freshness was what endeared this series to me. The same could be said of Rick Riordan's mashup of YA & Greek Myth but for some inexplicable reason, my interest in the Percy Jackson series was not sustained. Even then, Artemis Fowl remained a series that I was totally engrossed in. It is not usual to come across a criminal mastermind who is but a young boy dressed as if going to a funeral ! I have noticed those traces of freshness disappe</span>
  <span id="freeText1686922933244812043" style="display:none">There was an undeniable freshness to Artemis Fowl and this freshness was what endeared this series to me. The same could be said of Rick Riordan's mashup of YA &amp; Greek Myth but for some inexplicable reason, my interest in the Percy Jackson series was not sustained. Even then, Artemis Fowl remained a series that I was totally engrossed in. It is not usual to come across a criminal mastermind who is but a young boy dressed as if going to a funeral ! I have noticed those traces of freshness disappearing in the 6th book of the series and here it becomes a cliche ridden and extremely predictable story line.<br /><br />When asked about whether his Batman series would continue beyond a third film, Christopher Nolan had replied that there is only so much that you can stretch a character and its environs ( those were not the exact words but you get the picture don't you ? ). This applies for some series books for from being extremely entertaining to dreary dullness is the matter of just a few pages. Colfer is humorous and entertaining here but somehow this tale has an artificiality to it. Even in the thick of things, my mind kept telling me <i> This is pointless, go on and look at the book carefully. Did they put some other book between the covers ? </i> Alas, it was Artemis Fowl being made a cliche ! This one is way out of tune for such a brilliant series.<br /><br />That said, I am pretty positive that I will read the last installment as well. Two bad apples in a cart of five juicy ones is acceptable ain't it ? </span>
  <a data-text-id="1686922933244812043" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1564937049" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer2962474653913991059">This was a bit of a mixed bag for me. I love Artemis Fowl. Don't get me wrong. He was still quite humorous in this one, and I still enjoyed all the secondary characters' ingenuity and determination. I think it was going to be a tough thing for Colfer to portray mental illness in a good way with the cast of characters that he's working with, and I was right to a point. The characters treated the illness as a joke when Artemis was clearly suffering which didn't sit too well with me. I may just be </span>
  <span id="freeText2962474653913991059" style="display:none">This was a bit of a mixed bag for me. I love Artemis Fowl. Don't get me wrong. He was still quite humorous in this one, and I still enjoyed all the secondary characters' ingenuity and determination. I think it was going to be a tough thing for Colfer to portray mental illness in a good way with the cast of characters that he's working with, and I was right to a point. The characters treated the illness as a joke when Artemis was clearly suffering which didn't sit too well with me. I may just be being overly sensitive about it because I just read Challenger Deep, and the two characters go through similar thought process although they don't suffer from the same thing (obviously the mental illness in this is different &amp; made up and is a magical mental illness). And another thing that was weird was that Colfer gets a Greek myth about Artemis and Orion way wrong or used a version I could not find nor have ever heard of. But other than those two things, I found the journey fun and exciting. The pacing was fine as I finished this in less than a day. I think Colfer does some interesting things with poking fun of tropes which I thoroughly enjoyed. Looking forward to finishing the series with book 8!</span>
  <a data-text-id="2962474653913991059" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer6923573818677644857">I have enjoyed the Artemis Fowl series but this is a disappointing addition to the series. Artemis, ridden by guilt, has devised a system to combat global warming but in fact is in great danger from the Atlantis Complex - a multiple personality and OCD syndrome that is endangering his sanity when his fairy friends need his deviousness most.<br/><br/>The book itself acknowledges that it doesn't follow the usual pattern so don't expect any resolution. Consequently, it's surprisingly long considering this. U</span>
  <span id="freeText6923573818677644857" style="display:none">I have enjoyed the Artemis Fowl series but this is a disappointing addition to the series. Artemis, ridden by guilt, has devised a system to combat global warming but in fact is in great danger from the Atlantis Complex - a multiple personality and OCD syndrome that is endangering his sanity when his fairy friends need his deviousness most.<br /><br />The book itself acknowledges that it doesn't follow the usual pattern so don't expect any resolution. Consequently, it's surprisingly long considering this. Ultimately, this is a very funny read - Orion is a highly entertaining character and Foaly is his usual sarcastic self. Other than that I am waiting for the next one to resolve many of the events in this one.</span>

<div id="review_382367651" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/382367651" />
    <a title="Karel" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11497287-karel"><img alt="Karel" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1390489908p2/11497287.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/382367651?book_show_action=true">Aug 02, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Karel" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Karel" href="/user/show/11497287-karel">Karel</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11497287-karel?shelf=srzbznz">srzbznz</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer382367651" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3510648317111915646">A week ago, I'd think it's impossible for me to not like an AF book. Having just surfaced from this and the last book, I'm sorry to say that this is the weakest link in the entire series. And a very weak link it is.<br/><br/>The story starts out full of action - but none of it feels like the edge of the seat action found in previous books. In fact, it all feels like we're just hashing out routine. An explosion here, a crisis there. I find myself skipping whole paragraphs and then going back to read them o</span>
  <span id="freeText3510648317111915646" style="display:none">A week ago, I'd think it's impossible for me to not like an AF book. Having just surfaced from this and the last book, I'm sorry to say that this is the weakest link in the entire series. And a very weak link it is.<br /><br />The story starts out full of action - but none of it feels like the edge of the seat action found in previous books. In fact, it all feels like we're just hashing out routine. An explosion here, a crisis there. I find myself skipping whole paragraphs and then going back to read them out of duty. That was how unexciting it was - it felt like I was re-reading an old book for the thousandth time, with no interest in it at all.<br /><br />There's also a lot of wasted potential in the story. Orion, for example, could have been fleshed out to play a bigger part in the story. Instead, he's relegated to a hamming sideshow. He appears, pops a few funny lines, and then someone zaps him back to oblivion. Artemis too, is lacking of his characteristic master plans. That's understandable, of course, given his condition, but unfortunately, no one really steps up to fill in the void. <br /><br />As I've mentioned, the whole novel is pretty much one action scene after another. What's worse is that the action doesn't culminate in THE action scene. Instead, the climax is lukewarm, and if it wasn't for the appearance of THE villain, I wouldn't even recognize it as THE action scene. The ending was less a big bang than a white flag. <br /><br />The witty back-and-forth felt stale. No rolling on the floor laughing lines like the first few books here. Sometimes it even felt TOO back-and-forth, like the characters are rehearsed comedians.<br /><br />I'd sum the book out as 'meh', and you should read this if you're an AF fan, or just want to know it all for the upcoming finale. Those who are just picking up the book should start from the first one, or at the very least, the first few books.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3510648317111915646" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_205017893" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/205017893" />
    <a title="Emma" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5790306-emma"><img alt="Emma" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1314923666p2/5790306.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/205017893?book_show_action=true">Sep 03, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emma" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emma" href="/user/show/5790306-emma">Emma</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer205017893" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3549246529388884119">I was horribly disappointed with this book. Artemis Fowl has been one of my favorite series since middle school and I have always loved Colfer's voice and humor. But this book fell flat for me, it really did. First of all I didn't like how Artemis was either unconcious, insane, or was replaced by Orion (gag), for the entire novel. I know that this is purely personal opinion, but it really did ruin the book for me. Also, the plot was weak; I wasn't expecting this to happen at all. Colfer always h</span>
  <span id="freeText3549246529388884119" style="display:none">I was horribly disappointed with this book. Artemis Fowl has been one of my favorite series since middle school and I have always loved Colfer's voice and humor. But this book fell flat for me, it really did. First of all I didn't like how Artemis was either unconcious, insane, or was replaced by Orion (gag), for the entire novel. I know that this is purely personal opinion, but it really did ruin the book for me. Also, the plot was weak; I wasn't expecting this to happen at all. Colfer always has seat-of-your-pants plots with plenty of suspense, twists, and intruige. The Atlantis Complex had none of this. It was like he had completely run out of ideas and threw something together without putting any artistry into it at all. Character development was also really weak, which was another huge disappointment. Usually, Colfer's characters are well-defined and capture the readers attention; again, the Atlantis Complex didn't have this. I'm hoping he writes another, because this would be a horrible way to end an otherwise wonderful series, though I am a little afraid that another novel will recieve the same lack of artistry and effort that this one did. </span>
  <a data-text-id="3549246529388884119" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/116378569" />
    <a title="Alex Murphy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/993298-alex-murphy"><img alt="Alex Murphy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1583075248p2/993298.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/116378569?book_show_action=true">Aug 11, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alex Murphy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alex Murphy" href="/user/show/993298-alex-murphy">Alex Murphy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer116378569" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18389058007710404870">It's about time Colfer came out with another Fowl book!<br/><br/>Although the book was great I have to express my utter disappointment with the new jacket design. While the art is nice, you can't change an established title convention on book SEVEN of a series that is hitherto unchanged. It drives me crazy to see six books with the same font and template with one non-conforming book at the end. NOT okay, Hyperion.<br/><br/>Beyond my OCD, the book is great. Artemis's complex makes for a great new character addition.</span>
  <span id="freeText18389058007710404870" style="display:none">It's about time Colfer came out with another Fowl book!<br /><br />Although the book was great I have to express my utter disappointment with the new jacket design. While the art is nice, you can't change an established title convention on book SEVEN of a series that is hitherto unchanged. It drives me crazy to see six books with the same font and template with one non-conforming book at the end. NOT okay, Hyperion.<br /><br />Beyond my OCD, the book is great. Artemis's complex makes for a great new character addition. The prose, which is generally quite pretentious, is great here. His new (new? I don't remember him writing like this in the other ones, but maybe I wasn't paying attention) semi-absurdist, Family Guy-esque random humor is very well-placed (eg, "Turnball Root was famous for dealing with evidence and witnesses in a severe fashion. There was a legend going around the fairy fugitive bars that the captain had once burned down an entire shopping complex just to get rid of a thumbprint that he may have left behind in a booth at Falafel Fabulosity." pg. 225) and the whole book moves well. Our heros are back and ever-growing, which is great to see an author do (too many forget that, as time passes, people change). The villian is less exciting than villians of the previous books, but the whole package is quite worthwhile.<br /><br />In the next (and purportedly last) Artemis Fowl novel, there had better be no more ArtemisxHolly shipteasing, because we've been putting up with it for much too long. DTR, Colfer.<br /><br />Other than the unfortunate jacket mishap, a great book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18389058007710404870" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_165566896" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/165566896" />
    <a title="Jason" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4000000-jason"><img alt="Jason" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1278988144p2/4000000.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/165566896?book_show_action=true">May 04, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jason" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jason" href="/user/show/4000000-jason">Jason</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4000000-jason?shelf=fantasy-series">fantasy-series</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer165566896" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15597800648744098830">This was by far my least favorite Artemis book in the series. I don't know if I've just hit some sort of weird cosmic rut, but at least five of the books I've read this year which are parts of ongoing series have featured the main series protagonist being absent or fundamentally altered for a significant portion of the book. This one has Artemis experience a dissociative break very early on which lasts almost the length of the book. Much of the humor that the series is known for was absent as Co</span>
  <span id="freeText15597800648744098830" style="display:none">This was by far my least favorite Artemis book in the series. I don't know if I've just hit some sort of weird cosmic rut, but at least five of the books I've read this year which are parts of ongoing series have featured the main series protagonist being absent or fundamentally altered for a significant portion of the book. This one has Artemis experience a dissociative break very early on which lasts almost the length of the book. Much of the humor that the series is known for was absent as Colfer focused on giving proper gravitas to the torment of mental disease. Focusing on secondary characters and their quest to save the day without Artemis' help on the surface sounds like a recipe for avoiding stagnation in a fairly formulaic series for children, but in practice I felt a very large void because of Artemis' absence.<br /><br />The consequences have been graver and the resolutions have been messier and less conclusive as the series has progressed (Artemis himself even remarks upon this very thing in a meta acknowledgement by Colfer that his goal is to age the series). I'm happy that the characters have grown and changed over time, but the more adult the books become, the less I find myself enjoying them. I guess I don't see the problem with a series initially written for children staying firmly in the realm of children, but the modern trend towards aging a series along with the audience clearly disagrees with me.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15597800648744098830" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_98986799" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/98986799" />
    <a title="Anne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1720620-anne"><img alt="Anne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1415374035p2/1720620.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/98986799?book_show_action=true">Apr 17, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anne" href="/user/show/1720620-anne">Anne</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780141328027" href="/book/show/7913339-the-atlantis-complex">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=middle-grade-reader">middle-grade-reader</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=read-in-2010">read-in-2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer98986799&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer98986799" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11863073915539853447">Part of the fun of this series is that Artemis always has a scheme. Usually, a scam within a scheme. This time around...no scheme, no scam. In fact, no <i>Artemis</i>. Ok, in all fairness, Artemis <i>is</i> in this book, just not the Artemis that we know and love. Instead of the snarky boy genius with a tendency to lean toward criminal activity, we have a nice kid who feels guilty for all the wrong he has done in his life. Eh? <br/>Evidently, all the guilt (along with dabbling in fairy magic) has caused him to dev</span>
  <span id="freeText11863073915539853447" style="display:none">Part of the fun of this series is that Artemis always has a scheme. Usually, a scam within a scheme. This time around...no scheme, no scam. In fact, no <i>Artemis</i>. Ok, in all fairness, Artemis <i>is</i> in this book, just not the Artemis that we know and love. Instead of the snarky boy genius with a tendency to lean toward criminal activity, we have a nice kid who feels guilty for all the wrong he has done in his life. Eh? <br />Evidently, all the guilt (along with dabbling in fairy magic) has caused him to develop something called the Atlantis Complex. Which causes OCD-like symptoms, paranoia, and multiple personalities to emerge. Ok, that's not a bad premise for a story. Sounds good, right? Bzzzzzzt! Wrong! Why, you ask? Because Colfer never saw fit to <i>cure</i> him! He started out the book nuttier than a fruitcake, and in the closing pages he was sweetly shuffled off to the loony bin. <br />Now, I'm assuming that in the next book, this little problem will be rectified. However, it still doesn't change the fact that I read this entire book waiting for the <i>real</i> Artemis to pop up and say, "Gotcha! I was only faking! Mwahaha! Now let me show you how this was all part of my master plan!". Sadly, that never happened.<br />If this is the direction the series is taking, then I hope Colfer wraps it up after the next book. </span>
  <a data-text-id="11863073915539853447" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2279002040" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11995039066709401303"><i> That was a fun ride </i><br/><br/><b> OH GOD, NOW I AM SO SCARED TO END THIS SERIES....ONE MORE BOOK GEEEEEEZZZ >.< </b></span>

<div id="review_120853666" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/120853666" />
    <a title="Lori" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4268741-lori"><img alt="Lori" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/120853666?book_show_action=true">Sep 09, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lori" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lori" href="/user/show/4268741-lori">Lori</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer120853666" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12448810976853596307">I'm always up for a good mind-stimulating read, which is something I've always been able to depend on Colfer for. His books always kept me thinking, and his endings always got me to re-read his books again and again to try to catch every significant detail I might have missed hinting to the intricate twists and turns he weaves. I’ve grown to love the young yet enduringly intelligent Artemis Fowl; to have had to tolerate (and eventually I would go so far as to use the word ‘suffer’) through an en</span>
  <span id="freeText12448810976853596307" style="display:none">I'm always up for a good mind-stimulating read, which is something I've always been able to depend on Colfer for. His books always kept me thinking, and his endings always got me to re-read his books again and again to try to catch every significant detail I might have missed hinting to the intricate twists and turns he weaves. I’ve grown to love the young yet enduringly intelligent Artemis Fowl; to have had to tolerate (and eventually I would go so far as to use the word ‘suffer’) through an entire book lacking the usual flair was a terrible shame. Artemis’s trademark almost annoyingly-cocky-yet-endearing air (unfortunately replaced by a almost obnoxious, practically useless kid) and the story’s typical out-of-the-ashes victory only obtained by sheer wit and very detailed planning taking place throughout the entire story right within the text but floating completely unnoticed right through our minds was desperately missed. I found myself thinking time and time again throughout the book, “oh he’ll come through with some ingenious unforeseen plan!” only to be sorely disappointed. The usual twist in Colfer’s books was glaringly absent. This story was almost boring in relation to the previous installments; no spark, no satisfying ending leaving the reader in awe, no real indication that the next page would get much better. Nevermind Artemis’s genius being inhibited by the OCD he contracts; Colfer’s own genius gets smothered in this novel. It was a sad day to finish an Artemis Fowl book without thinking “this guy really IS a genius.”</span>
  <a data-text-id="12448810976853596307" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2921582231" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16796647359546976216">*sigh*<br/><br/>This might sound bad, but this is the book that ruined my life. XD<br/><br/>In a good way! (I think.)<br/><br/>I’ll try to explain why I love this book so much.<br/><br/>For the first six books of the series, we meet Artemis Fowl. Genius. Criminal mastermind. Teenager. We see bits and pieces of his humanity as the series goes along, although usually the plot returns to saving the world.<br/><br/>We always see Artemis Fowl as this invincible person - at least in the mind, anyways.<br/><br/>But this book just throws all that out the window </span>
  <span id="freeText16796647359546976216" style="display:none">*sigh*<br /><br />This might sound bad, but this is the book that ruined my life. XD<br /><br />In a good way! (I think.)<br /><br />I’ll try to explain why I love this book so much.<br /><br />For the first six books of the series, we meet Artemis Fowl. Genius. Criminal mastermind. Teenager. We see bits and pieces of his humanity as the series goes along, although usually the plot returns to saving the world.<br /><br />We always see Artemis Fowl as this invincible person - at least in the mind, anyways.<br /><br />But this book just throws all that out the window and replaces it with a plot of Artemis . . . kind of going insane. And it is FASCINATING. (Not in a creepy way.) Atlantis Complex is the type of fictional illness that I both want to see in action in real life and also never want anyone to get.<br /><br />Seeing Artemis struggle with this, which is caused by guilt, is just . . . it’s very fresh. And it shows his humanity in a way that none of the other books could - through fighting something that is messing with the one thing he trusts most, his intellect.<br /><br />Also, this might sound bad, but Artemis with Atlantis Complex is just downright FUNNY. All those Orion sequences? (Orion is a dual personality brought on by Atlantis.) Yeah, you’ll never take Artemis seriously again. XD<br /><br />(Just a side note: every time I finish this book I catch a small version of Atlantis Complex. Yes, I’m counting my words. ;) )<br /><br />It’s a pretty clean book, unless you count these hysterical snippets as “not appropriate”:<br /><br />Orion: *to Holly* “Oh I’m crazy all right. Multiple psychosis, paranoia, OCD. I’ve got them all, but most of all, I’m crazy about you.”<br />Foaly: “That’s actually not a bad line. He is definitely not Artemis.”<br /><br />Artemis: “I’m the nut. I’m the nut!”<br /><br />Artemis: *ten minutes after reciting number poetry* “Number poetry? That’s ridiculous.”<br /><br />May the fives be with you all. ;)</span>
  <a data-text-id="16796647359546976216" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_382886527" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/382886527" />
    <a title="Mandy Jo" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6268517-mandy-jo"><img alt="Mandy Jo" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1334714867p2/6268517.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/382886527?book_show_action=true">Aug 02, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mandy Jo" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mandy Jo" href="/user/show/6268517-mandy-jo">Mandy Jo</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6268517-mandy-jo?shelf=litr%C3%ADocht-na-h%C3%A9ireann">litríocht-na-héireann</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer382886527" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14120093966354582689"><br/><b>This week’s headline?</b> "Love and magic."<br/><br/><b>Why this book?</b> to read finale<br/><br/><b>Which book format?</b> from the library<br/><br/><b>Primary reading environment?</b> bedtime at home<br/><br/><b>Any preconceived notions?</b> it's Artemis Fowl<br/><br/><b>Identify most with?</b> "LEP ninja training." <br/><br/><b>Three little words?</b> "Follow those bubbles."<br/><br/><b>Goes well with?</b> "Mmm, horse. Tasty."<br/><br/><b>Recommend this to?</b> "dolphins, little ones"<br/><br/>I'm a bit too old for these books, so the character of Mulch Diggums doesn't thrill me as much as he does the little kids, but there was one scene </span>
  <span id="freeText14120093966354582689" style="display:none"><br /><b>This week’s headline?</b> "Love and magic."<br /><br /><b>Why this book?</b> to read finale<br /><br /><b>Which book format?</b> from the library<br /><br /><b>Primary reading environment?</b> bedtime at home<br /><br /><b>Any preconceived notions?</b> it's Artemis Fowl<br /><br /><b>Identify most with?</b> "LEP ninja training." <br /><br /><b>Three little words?</b> "Follow those bubbles."<br /><br /><b>Goes well with?</b> "Mmm, horse. Tasty."<br /><br /><b>Recommend this to?</b> "dolphins, little ones"<br /><br />I'm a bit too old for these books, so the character of Mulch Diggums doesn't thrill me as much as he does the little kids, but there was one scene with Mulch that had me shaking with laughter:<br /><blockquote>"Hey, look," said Mulch, once the air lock had drained. "It's the nut." He ran in small circles around the bay, squealing, "I'm the nut. I'm the nut." The dwarf stopped for a laugh. "He cracks me up, really."</blockquote><br />Okay, I suppose that doesn't make much sense out of context, but it was so silly that I couldn't stop giggling. <br /><br />The Fowl twins are also good for a laugh, though they never actually appeared in this adventure. The technology was very good, and I loved that the story started off in a world where all teenagers care deeply about the environment.<br /><br />It's been a few years since I read the rest of the series (since <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2179276.The_Time_Paradox__Artemis_Fowl___6_" title="The Time Paradox (Artemis Fowl, #6) by Eoin Colfer" rel="nofollow noopener">The Time Paradox</a> was released, in 2008), so I needed to catch up in order to read the finale that just came out. This might be the first book I've read since the makeover, which I guess has something to do with the Disney logo on the spine and back flap?<br /><br />I have to admit, I sometimes wish there was more romance. Artemis is 15, a boy genius, and Irish, but he rarely thinks about girls. Sometimes it feels like I'm just reading to follow the tension building between him and Holly.<br /><br />In that way, I'm almost glad nothing has ever come of it. Holly going on a date with Commander Trouble Kelp, and Artemis asking her about it - subtly, jokingly, and just the once - it's almost like these two are so concerned with saving the world that they are going to miss out on each other.<br /><br /><b>Other cultural accompaniments:</b> The first six Artemis Fowl books.<br /><br /><b>Grade:</b> B+<br /><br /><b>I leave you with this:</b> "Holly did not answer, but with that touch, No1 felt the rune spell that squatted like a parasite on her mind. It seemed purple to him, and malignant, and somehow aware. In his imagination, the reptilian rune crouching on Holly's brain snarled at him and nipped with venomous teeth."</span>
  <a data-text-id="14120093966354582689" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_118522544" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/118522544" />
    <a title="Alexandra" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2598584-alexandra"><img alt="Alexandra" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1479388521p2/2598584.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/118522544?book_show_action=true">Aug 25, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alexandra" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alexandra" href="/user/show/2598584-alexandra">Alexandra</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780141328041" href="/book/show/7913340-the-atlantis-complex">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer118522544" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16280158255123629605">There's something definitely lacking in this book. Oh, it's still witty, it still made me laugh in the most delightful ways, and it's still got heart among all the action and explosions. There's nothing I love more than a reformed brilliant criminal mastermind (this is my favorite trope actually) and watching Artemis try to become good and swallowed with guilt and not disappoint his mother anymore was heartbreaking. <br/><br/>And the ever-subtle love story! If it's true that the next book is going to be t</span>
  <span id="freeText16280158255123629605" style="display:none">There's something definitely lacking in this book. Oh, it's still witty, it still made me laugh in the most delightful ways, and it's still got heart among all the action and explosions. There's nothing I love more than a reformed brilliant criminal mastermind (this is my favorite trope actually) and watching Artemis try to become good and swallowed with guilt and not disappoint his mother anymore was heartbreaking. <br /><br />And the ever-subtle love story! If it's true that the next book is going to be the last, I would really really like that to be resolved. Of course, Orion was the one who said everything that Artemis couldn't have said himself to Holly, but how could they not deal with it at all in the aftermath? I wish they'd at least talked about that, because it wasn't as if Orion was an entirely different person.<br /><br />But yes, action-wise, it was a bit lacking. No brilliant twists this time and frankly the villain was a bit boring to me. As much as I think Opal gets way too many comebacks, she always delivers the best performance and the books with her in it are my favorites. It seems like no one else just can measure up to her amazing plots. So yeah, this book was a little of a letdown compared to the previous ones. And there's something that just isn't right with seeing Artemis not his usual brilliant self. Let's hope this changes in the next book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16280158255123629605" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_118173909" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/118173909" />
    <a title="Arnav" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4191017-arnav"><img alt="Arnav" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/118173909?book_show_action=true">Aug 23, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Arnav" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Arnav" href="/user/show/4191017-arnav">Arnav</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer118173909&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer118173909" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1026567349848091884">I'm a die hard Artemis fan, and after reading (and owning) the last six books, I eagerly awaited the Atlantis Complex and went off specifically to purchase it on its release date in India.<br/><br/>The first chapter showed that the book would go off on a good note, but the rest of the chapters, were simply fillers to the book's 323 or 357 pages (depending on the publisher). Honestly, the book lacked the rich fairy tale luster in the previous books. It was a disappointment to see the series end up in this </span>
  <span id="freeText1026567349848091884" style="display:none">I'm a die hard Artemis fan, and after reading (and owning) the last six books, I eagerly awaited the Atlantis Complex and went off specifically to purchase it on its release date in India.<br /><br />The first chapter showed that the book would go off on a good note, but the rest of the chapters, were simply fillers to the book's 323 or 357 pages (depending on the publisher). Honestly, the book lacked the rich fairy tale luster in the previous books. It was a disappointment to see the series end up in this fashion. The storyline was not solid, as it was in the all the previous books and the end did not have a twist. It simply ended on a drab note with Artemis finding himself with Foaly and Holly at his bedside. The book was neither moving nor was it emotional. Colfer tried to mix Orion's puberty with his attitude, but the result was bland and tasteless. Had I not been such a great fan of the Artemis Fowl's series, this book wouldn't have gotten more than 2/5<br /><br />Colfer (my favorite author) should really rethink the future of the Artemis Fowl series. </span>
  <a data-text-id="1026567349848091884" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Zpi/F36lUvtutO2fKf2ZtKIvU2wF/yRzF5lMzKMXJGxcvtbFxfubk8mfWf7eCJNrdHC0pMtyqhRM5wp9blTW9g==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('3aMvEmmRVj4K9En0ZoiOvtVHwHDm7EbVZyvYLtliFILnhUbA0s+fVq3f/ZWRfYRhAxgnuChhyLI8VZ6fFCHmGA==')})
  }

<span id="freeTextContainer9729095579982382729">Eoin Colfer (pronounced Owen) was born in Wexford on the South-East coast of Ireland in 1965, where he and his four brothers were brought up by his father and mother, who were both educators.<br/><br/>He received his degree from Dublin University and began teaching primary school in Wexford. He has lived and worked all over the world, including Saudi Arabia, Tunisia and Italy. After the publication of the A</span>
  <span id="freeText9729095579982382729" style="display:none">Eoin Colfer (pronounced Owen) was born in Wexford on the South-East coast of Ireland in 1965, where he and his four brothers were brought up by his father and mother, who were both educators.<br /><br />He received his degree from Dublin University and began teaching primary school in Wexford. He has lived and worked all over the world, including Saudi Arabia, Tunisia and Italy. After the publication of the Artemis Fowl novels, Eoin retired from teaching and now writes full time. He lives in Ireland with his wife and two children.<br /><br /></span>
